## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task belongs to chemical reaction kinetics, modeling the instantaneous rate of change of concentration (dA_dt) as a function of concentration (A) and time (t). The relationships typically follow rate laws determined by reaction order, reversibility, autocatalysis, or time-dependent factors like catalyst deactivation or changing environmental conditions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate limited by catalyst surface or irradiance)
- First-order unimolecular decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (simple decomposition or radioactive decay)
- Second-order bimolecular collision: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (reaction between two identical species)
- General nth-order power law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order fitting)
- Reversible approach to equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (net flux driven by distance from equilibrium)
- Autocatalytic feedback: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product accelerates formation until depletion)
- Catalyst deactivation model: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-dependent rate constant decay/growth)
- Diffusion-controlled encounter: dA_dt = c0 * A * t**c1 (time-dependent rate coefficient in Smoluchowski regime)
- Ignition threshold kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * (A - c1)**c2 (rate activates only above critical concentration)
- Parallel competing pathways: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * A**c3 (simultaneous reactions of different orders)
- Time-modulated batch process: dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 + c1 * t)**c2 (changing conditions like temperature or mixing over time)
- Oscillatory autocatalysis: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A + c2 * A**2) (nonlinear feedback in oscillating chemical systems)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Constant rate despite concentration drop â†’ Zero-order kinetics (rate-limited by catalyst surface area or light intensity)
- Quadratic or higher power concentration dependence â†’ Bimolecular/termolecular collision frequency scaling
- Rate proportional to distance from equilibrium concentration â†’ Reversible reaction net flux
- Unimodal (bell-shaped) rate profile vs concentration â†’ Autocatalytic feedback with reactant depletion
- Explicit time modulation of concentration dependence â†’ Catalyst deactivation, temperature ramp, or diffusion front evolution
- Multi-power concentration summation â†’ Parallel competing reaction pathways
- Time-fractional power law dependence â†’ Diffusion-controlled encounters in heterogeneous media
- Cubic polynomial rate expression â†’ Nonlinear oscillatory feedback in complex mechanistic networks

### Analysis of Candidates vs Ground Truth

**Ground Truth (GT) Structure:**
The GT expression is `-c0*A**c1 + c2*_m*sin(sqrt(A))`. Given `c1 = 2.0`, this simplifies to a linear combination of exactly two basis functions:
1. `A**2` (quadratic term)
2. `sin(sqrt(A))` (sine of the square root of A)

There are no constant terms, linear `A` terms, `A**(1/3)` terms, logarithmic terms, or exponential terms in the GT. Any candidate must be algebraically reducible to exactly `C1 * A**2 + C2 * sin(sqrt(A))` by setting its free constants appropriately.

**Candidate Evaluation:**
- **Basis Function Mismatch:** The GT contains `sin(sqrt(A))`. None of the 69 candidates contain `sin(sqrt(A))`, `sin(A**0.5)`, or `sin(c*sqrt(A))`. Candidates use `sin(A*c + d)` (linear argument), `sin(log(...))`, `sin(exp(...))`, or `log/cos/exp` functions, which are linearly independent from `sin(sqrt(A))` and cannot be transformed into it via constant assignment.
- **Polynomial Structure Mismatch:** Many candidates (e.g., 1, 12, 17, 23, 27, 42, 45, 66, 68) are rational functions where the denominator `(A + c)` or `(A*c + 1)` prevents exact reduction to a pure `A**2` term without introducing unwanted rational dependencies or limiting the domain. Candidates that successfully isolate `A**2` (e.g., 51, 56, 57, 58 via cancellation) lack any trigonometric component entirely.
- **Extra Terms:** Candidates like 3, 6, 7, 10, 22, 34, 44, 51, 56, 57, 58 contain `A**(1/3)` or `log(A)` or `exp(A)` terms that cannot be zeroed out to match the GT's exact two-term structure.
- **Domain Constraints:** While `Abs(A)` can be treated as `A` for `A >= 0`, this only applies to absolute values inside polynomials or roots (e.g., Candidates 25, 26, 47). Even with this relaxation, these candidates feature `sqrt(A)` or `sqrt(A+c)` as standalone terms, not inside a `sin()` function, and thus fail to match `sin(sqrt(A))`.

**Conclusion:**
No candidate possesses the required `sin(sqrt(A))` basis function, nor can any candidate be algebraically manipulated to exactly match the GT's structure of `C1*A**2 + C2*sin(sqrt(A))`.
